attempts to interpret the given traversal as a\n// \"move endpoint\" address, which is a relative path from the module containing\n// the traversal to a movable object in either the same module or in some\n// child module.\n//\n// This deals only with the syntactic element of a move endpoint expression\n// in configuration. Before the result will be useful you'll need to combine\n// it with the address of the module where it was declared in order to get\n// an absolute address relative to the root module.\nfunc ParseMoveEndpoint(traversal hcl.Traversal) (*MoveEndpoint, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tpath, remain, diags := parseModuleInstancePrefix(traversal)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\trng := tfdiags.SourceRangeFromHCL(traversal.SourceRange())\n\n\tif len(remain) == 0 {\n\t\treturn &MoveEndpoint{\n\t\t\trelSubject:  path,\n\t\t\tSourceRange: rng,\n\t\t}, diags\n\t}\n\n\triAddr, moreDiags := parseResourceInstanceUnderModule(path, remain)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\treturn &MoveEndpoint{\n\t\trelSubject:  riAddr,\n\t\tSourceRange: rng,\n\t}, diags\n}\n\n// UnifyMoveEndpoints takes a pair of MoveEndpoint objects representing the\n// \"from\" and \"to\" addresses in a moved block, and returns a pair of\n// MoveEndpointInModule addresses guaranteed to be of the same dynamic type\n// that represent what the two MoveEndpoint addresses refer to.\n//\n// moduleAddr must be the address of the module where the move was declared.\n//\n// This function deals both with the conversion from relative to absolute\n// addresses and with resolving the ambiguity between no-key instance\n// addresses and whole-object addresses, returning the least specific\n// address type possible.\n//\n// Not all combinations of addresses are unifyable: the two addresses must\n// either both include resources or both just be modules. If the two\n// given addresses are incompatible then UnifyMoveEndpoints returns (nil, nil),\n// in which case the caller should typically report an error to the user\n// stating the unification constraints.\nfunc UnifyMoveEndpoints(moduleAddr Module, relFrom, relTo *MoveEndpoint) (modFrom, modTo *MoveEndpointInModule) {\n\n\t// First we'll make a decision about which address type we're\n\t// ultimately trying to unify to. For our internal purposes\n\t// here we're going to borrow TargetableAddrType just as a\n\t// convenient way to talk about our address types, even though\n\t// targetable address types are not 100% aligned with moveable\n\t// address types.\n\tfromType := relFrom.internalAddrType()\n\ttoType := relTo.internalAddrType()\n\tvar wantType TargetableAddrType\n\n\t// Our goal here is to choose the whole-resource or whole-module-call\n\t// addresses if both agree on it, but to use specific instance addresses\n\t// otherwise. This is a somewhat-arbitrary way to resolve syntactic\n\t// ambiguity between the two situations which allows both for renaming\n\t// whole resources and for switching from a single-instance object to\n\t// a multi-instance object.\n\tswitch {\n\tcase fromType == AbsResourceInstanceAddrType || toType == AbsResourceInstanceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = AbsResourceInstanceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == AbsResourceAddrType || toType == AbsResourceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = AbsResourceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == ModuleInstanceAddrType || toType == ModuleInstanceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = ModuleInstanceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == ModuleAddrType || toType == ModuleAddrType:\n\t\t// NOTE: We're fudging a little here and using\n\t\t// ModuleAddrType to represent AbsModuleCall rather\n\t\t// than Module.\n\t\twantType = ModuleAddrType\n\tdefault:\n\t\tpanic(\"unhandled move address types\")\n\t}\n\n\tmodFrom = relFrom.prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr, wantType)\n\tmodTo = relTo.prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr, wantType)\n\tif modFrom == nil || modTo == nil {\n\t\t// if either of them failed then they both failed, to make the\n\t\t// caller's life a little easier.\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\treturn modFrom, modTo\n}\n\nfunc (e *MoveEndpoint) prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr Module, wantType TargetableAddrType) *MoveEndpointInModule {\n\t// relAddr can only be either AbsResourceInstance or ModuleInstance, the\n\t// internal intermediate representation produced by ParseMoveEndpoint.\n\trelAddr := e.relSubject\n\n\tswitch relAddr rewrap this one.\n\t\t\treturn &MoveEndpointInModule{\n\t\t\t\tSourceRange: e.SourceRange,\n\t\t\t\tmodule:      moduleAddr,\n\t\t\t\trelSubject:  relAddr,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase ModuleAddrType:\n\t\t\t// NOTE: We're fudging a little here and using\n\t\t\t// ModuleAddrType to represent AbsModuleCall rather\n\t\t\t// than Module.\n\t\t\tcallerAddr, callAddr := relAddr.Call()\n\t\t\tabsCallAddr := AbsModuleCall{\n\t\t\t\tModule: callerAddr,\n\t\t\t\tCall:   callAddr,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn &MoveEndpointInModule{\n\t\t\t\tSourceRange: e.SourceRange,\n\t\t\t\tmodule:      moduleAddr,\n\t\t\t\trelSubject:  absCallAddr,\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\treturn nil // can't make any other types from a ModuleInstance\n\t\t}\n\tcase AbsResourceInstance:\n\t\tswitch wantType relAddr.ContainingResource(),\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\treturn nil // can't make any other types from an AbsResourceInstance\n\t\t}\n\tdefault:\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unhandled address type %T\", relAddr))\n\t}\n}\n\n// internalAddrType helps facilitate our slight abuse of TargetableAddrType\n// as a way to talk about our different possible result address types in\n// e.relSubject.(type) {\n\tcase ModuleInstance:\n\t\tif !addr.IsRoot() && addr[len(addr)-1].InstanceKey == NoKey {\n\t\t\t// NOTE: We're fudging a little here and using\n\t\t\t// ModuleAddrType to represent AbsModuleCall rather\n\t\t\t// than Module.\n\t\t\treturn ModuleAddrType\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn ModuleInstanceAddrType\n\tcase AbsResourceInstance:\n\t\tif addr.Resource.Key == NoKey values.\n\t\treturn e.String() == other.String() && e.SourceRange == other.SourceRange\n\t}\n}\n\n// MightUnifyWith returns true if it is possible that a later call to\n// UnifyMoveEndpoints might succeed if given the reciever and the other\n// given endpoint.\n//\n// This is intended for early static validation of obviously-wrong situations,\n// although there are still various semantic errors that this cannot catch.\nfunc (e *MoveEndpoint) MightUnifyWith(other *MoveEndpoint) bool {\n\t// For our purposes here we'll just do a unify without a base module\n\t// address, because the rules for whether unify can succeed depend\n\t// only on the relative part of the addresses, not on which module\n\t// they were declared in.\n\tfrom, to := UnifyMoveEndpoints(RootModule, e, other)\n\treturn from != nil && to != nil\n}\n\n// ConfigMoveable transforms the reciever into a ConfigMoveable by resolving it\n// relative to the given base module, which should be the module where\n// the MoveEndpoint expression was found.\n//\n// The result is useful for finding the target object in the configuration,\n// but it's not sufficient for fully interpreting a move statement because\n// it addr.Module.Module()...)\n\t\treturn ConfigResource{\n\t\t\tModule:   moduleAddr,\n\t\t\tResource: addr.Resource.Resource,\n\t\t}\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// The above should be exhaustive for all of the types\n\t\t// that ParseMoveEndpoint produces as our intermediate\n\t\t// address representation.\n\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported address type %T\", addr))\n\t}\n\n}\n\n// ParseMoveEndpoint attempts to interpret the given traversal as a\n// \"move endpoint\" address, which is a relative path from the module containing\n// the traversal to a movable object in either the same module or in some\n// child module.\n//\n// This deals only with the syntactic element of a move endpoint expression\n// in configuration. Before the result will be useful you'll need to combine\n// it with the address of the module where it was declared in order to get\n// an absolute address relative to the root module.\nfunc ParseMoveEndpoint(traversal hcl.Traversal) (*MoveEndpoint, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tpath, remain, diags := parseModuleInstancePrefix(traversal, false)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\trng := tfdiags.SourceRangeFromHCL(traversal.SourceRange())\n\n\tif len(remain) == 0 {\n\t\treturn &MoveEndpoint{\n\t\t\trelSubject:  path,\n\t\t\tSourceRange: rng,\n\t\t}, diags\n\t}\n\n\triAddr, moreDiags := parseResourceInstanceUnderModule(path, false, remain)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(moreDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\treturn nil, diags\n\t}\n\n\treturn &MoveEndpoint{\n\t\trelSubject:  riAddr,\n\t\tSourceRange: rng,\n\t}, diags\n}\n\n// UnifyMoveEndpoints takes a pair of MoveEndpoint objects representing the\n// \"from\" and \"to\" addresses in a moved block, and returns a pair of\n// MoveEndpointInModule addresses guaranteed to be of the same dynamic type\n// that represent what the two MoveEndpoint addresses refer to.\n//\n// moduleAddr must be the address of the module where the move was declared.\n//\n// This function deals both with the conversion from relative to absolute\n// addresses and with resolving the ambiguity between no-key instance\n// addresses and whole-object addresses, returning the least specific\n// address type possible.\n//\n// Not all combinations of addresses are unifyable: the two addresses must\n// either both include resources or both just be modules. If the two\n// given addresses are incompatible then UnifyMoveEndpoints returns (nil, nil),\n// in which case the caller should typically report an error to the user\n// stating the unification constraints.\nfunc UnifyMoveEndpoints(moduleAddr Module, relFrom, relTo *MoveEndpoint) (modFrom, modTo *MoveEndpointInModule) {\n\n\t// First we'll make a decision about which address type we're\n\t// ultimately trying to unify to. For our internal purposes\n\t// here we're going to borrow TargetableAddrType just as a\n\t// convenient way to talk about our address types, even though\n\t// targetable address types are not 100% aligned with moveable\n\t// address types.\n\tfromType := relFrom.internalAddrType()\n\ttoType := relTo.internalAddrType()\n\tvar wantType TargetableAddrType\n\n\t// Our goal here is to choose the whole-resource or whole-module-call\n\t// addresses if both agree on it, but to use specific instance addresses\n\t// otherwise. This is a somewhat-arbitrary way to resolve syntactic\n\t// ambiguity between the two situations which allows both for renaming\n\t// whole resources and for switching from a single-instance object to\n\t// a multi-instance object.\n\tswitch {\n\tcase fromType == AbsResourceInstanceAddrType || toType == AbsResourceInstanceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = AbsResourceInstanceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == AbsResourceAddrType || toType == AbsResourceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = AbsResourceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == ModuleInstanceAddrType || toType == ModuleInstanceAddrType:\n\t\twantType = ModuleInstanceAddrType\n\tcase fromType == ModuleAddrType || toType == ModuleAddrType:\n\t\t// NOTE: We're fudging a little here and using\n\t\t// ModuleAddrType to represent AbsModuleCall rather\n\t\t// than Module.\n\t\twantType = ModuleAddrType\n\tdefault:\n\t\tpanic(\"unhandled move address types\")\n\t}\n\n\tmodFrom = relFrom.prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr, wantType)\n\tmodTo = relTo.prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr, wantType)\n\tif modFrom == nil || modTo == nil {\n\t\t// if either of them failed then they both failed, to make the\n\t\t// caller's life a little easier.\n\t\treturn nil, nil\n\t}\n\treturn modFrom, modTo\n}\n\nfunc (e *MoveEndpoint) prepareMoveEndpointInModule(moduleAddr Module, wantType TargetableAddrType) *MoveEndpointInModule The type of the result conforms\n// to the implied type of the given schema.\n//\n// This function does not automatically expand \"dynamic\" blocks within the\n// body. If that is desired, first call the ExpandBlock method to obtain\n// an expanded body to pass to this method.\n//\n// If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the result may be\n// incomplete or invalid.\nfunc (s *Scope) EvalBlock(body hcl.Body, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n\tspec := schema.DecoderSpec()\n\n\trefs, diags := langrefs.ReferencesInBlock(s.ParseRef, body, schema)\n\n\tctx, ctxDiags := s.EvalContext(refs)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(ctxDiags)\n\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n\t\t// We'll stop early if we found problems in the references, because\n\t\t// it's likely evaluation will produce redundant copies of the same errors.\n\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(schema.ImpliedType()), diags\n\t}\n\n\t// HACK: In order to remain compatible with some assumptions made in\n\t// Terraform v0.11 and earlier about the approximate equivalence of\n\t// attribute vs. block syntax, we do a just-in-time fixup here to allow\n\t// any attribute in the schema that has a list-of-objects or set-of-objects\n\t// kind to potentially be populated instead by one or more nested blocks\n\t// whose type is the attribute name.\n\tbody = blocktoattr.FixUpBlockAttrs(body, schema)\n\n\tval, evalDiags := hcldec.Decode(body, spec, ctx)\n\tdiags = diags.Append(checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(evalDiags))\n\n\treturn val, diags\n}\n\n// EvalSelfBlock evaluates the given body only within the scope of the provided\n// object and instance key data. References to the object must use self, and the\n// key data will only contain count.index or each.key. The static values for\n// terraform and path will also be available in this context.\nfunc (s *Scope) EvalSelfBlock(body hcl.Body, self cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block, keyData cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n\t\t\t\"key\": keyData.EachKey,\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\n\trefs, refDiags := langrefs.References(s.ParseRef, hcldec.Variables(body, spec))\n\tdiags = diags.Append(refDiags)\n\n\tterraformAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n\tpathAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n\n\t// We could always load the static values for Path and Terraform values,\n\t// but we want to parse the references so that we can get source ranges for\n\t// user diagnostics.\n\tfor _, ref := range refs {\n\t\t// we already loaded the self value\n\t\tif ref.Subject == addrs.Self {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tswitch subj := ref.Subject.(type) {\n\t\tcase addrs.PathAttr:\n\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetPathAttr(subj, ref.SourceRange))\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n\t\t\tpathAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n\n\t\tcase addrs.TerraformAttr:\n\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetTerraformAttr(subj, ref.SourceRange))\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n\t\t\tterraformAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n\n\t\tcase addrs.CountAttr, addrs.ForEachAttr:\n\t\t\t// each and count have already been handled.\n\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t// This should have been caught in validation, but point the user\n\t\t\t// to the correct location in case something slipped through.\n\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Invalid reference`,\n\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"The reference to %q is not valid in this context\", ref.Subject),\n\t\t\t\tSubject: diags\n}\n\n// EvalExpr evaluates a single expression in the receiving context and returns\n// the resulting value. If that is desired, first call the ExpandBlock method to obtain\n    50→// an expanded body to pass to this method.\n    51→//\n    52→// If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the result may be\n    53→// incomplete or invalid.\n    54→func (s *Scope) EvalBlock(body hcl.Body, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    55→\tspec := schema.DecoderSpec()\n    56→\n    57→\trefs, diags := langrefs.ReferencesInBlock(s.ParseRef, body, schema)\n    58→\n    59→\tctx, ctxDiags := s.EvalContext(refs)\n    60→\tdiags = diags.Append(ctxDiags)\n    61→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n    62→\t\t// We'll stop early if we found problems in the references, because\n    63→\t\t// it's likely evaluation will produce redundant copies of the same errors.\n    64→\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(schema.ImpliedType()), diags\n    65→\t}\n    66→\n    67→\t// HACK: In order to remain compatible with some assumptions made in\n    68→\t// Terraform v0.11 and earlier about the approximate equivalence of\n    69→\t// attribute vs. block syntax, we do a just-in-time fixup here to allow\n    70→\t// any attribute in the schema that has a list-of-objects or set-of-objects\n    71→\t// kind to potentially be populated instead by one or more nested blocks\n    72→\t// whose type is the attribute name.\n    73→\tbody = blocktoattr.FixUpBlockAttrs(body, schema)\n    74→\n    75→\tval, evalDiags := hcldec.Decode(body, spec, ctx)\n    76→\tdiags = diags.Append(checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(evalDiags))\n    77→\n    78→\treturn val, diags\n    79→}\n    80→\n    81→// EvalSelfBlock evaluates the given body only within the scope of the provided\n    82→// object and instance key data. References to the object must use self, and the\n    83→// key data will only contain count.index or each.key. The static values for\n    84→// terraform and path will also be available in this context.\n    85→func (s *Scope) EvalSelfBlock(body hcl.Body, self cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block, keyData instances.RepetitionData) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    86→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    87→\n    88→\tspec := schema.DecoderSpec()\n    89→\n    90→\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n    91→\tvals[\"self\"] = self\n    92→\n    93→\tif !keyData.CountIndex.IsNull() {\n    94→\t\tvals[\"count\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n    95→\t\t\t\"index\": keyData.CountIndex,\n    96→\t\t})\n    97→\t}\n    98→\tif !keyData.EachKey.IsNull() {\n    99→\t\tvals[\"each\"] = cty.ObjectVal(map[string]cty.Value{\n   100→\t\t\t\"key\": keyData.EachKey,\n   101→\t\t})\n   102→\t}\n   103→\n   104→\trefs, refDiags := langrefs.References(s.ParseRef, hcldec.Variables(body, spec))\n   105→\tdiags = diags.Append(refDiags)\n   106→\n   107→\tterraformAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   108→\tpathAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   109→\n   110→\t// We could always load the static values for Path and Terraform values,\n   111→\t// but we want to parse the references so that we can get source ranges for\n   112→\t// user diagnostics.\n   113→\tfor _, ref := range refs {\n   114→\t\t// we already loaded the self value\n   115→\t\tif ref.Subject == addrs.Self {\n   116→\t\t\tcontinue\n   117→\t\t}\n   118→\n   119→\t\tswitch subj := ref.Subject.(type) {\n   120→\t\tcase addrs.PathAttr:\n   121→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetPathAttr(subj, ref.SourceRange))\n   122→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   123→\t\t\tpathAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   124→\n   125→\t\tcase addrs.TerraformAttr:\n   126→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetTerraformAttr(subj, ref.SourceRange))\n   127→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   128→\t\t\tterraformAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   129→\n   130→\t\tcase addrs.CountAttr, addrs.ForEachAttr:\n   131→\t\t\t// each and count have already been handled.\n   132→\n   133→\t\tdefault:\n   134→\t\t\t// This should have been caught in validation, but point the user\n   135→\t\t\t// to the correct location in case something slipped through.\n   136→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   137→\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   138→\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Invalid reference`,\n   139→\t\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"The reference to %q is not valid in this context\", ref.Subject),\n   140→\t\t\t\tSubject:  ref.SourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   141→\t\t\t})\n   142→\t\t}\n   143→\t}\n   144→\n   145→\tvals[\"path\"] = cty.ObjectVal(pathAttrs)\n   146→\tvals[\"terraform\"] = cty.ObjectVal(terraformAttrs)\n   147→\n   148→\tctx := &hcl.EvalContext{\n   149→\t\tVariables: vals,\n   150→\t\tFunctions: s.Functions(),\n   151→\t}\n   152→\n   153→\tval, decDiags := hcldec.Decode(body, schema.DecoderSpec(), ctx)\n   154→\tdiags = diags.Append(checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(decDiags))\n   155→\treturn val, diags\n   156→}\n   157→\n   158→// EvalExpr evaluates a single expression in the receiving context and returns\n   159→// the resulting value. The value will be converted to the given type before\n   160→// it is returned if possible, or else an error diagnostic will be produced\n   161→// describing the conversion error.\n   162→//\n   163→// Pass an expected type of cty.DynamicPseudoType to skip automatic conversion\n   164→// and just obtain the returned value directly.\n   165→//\n   166→// If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the result may be\n   167→// incomplete, but will always be of the requested type.\n   168→func (s *Scope) EvalExpr(expr hcl.Expression, wantType cty.Type) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   169→\trefs, diags := langrefs.ReferencesInExpr(s.ParseRef, expr)\n   170→\n   171→\tctx, ctxDiags := s.EvalContext(refs)\n   172→\tdiags = diags.Append(ctxDiags)\n   173→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   174→\t\t// We'll stop early if we found problems in the references, because\n   175→\t\t// it's likely evaluation will produce redundant copies of the same errors.\n   176→\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(wantType), diags\n   177→\t}\n   178→\n   179→\tval, evalDiags := expr.Value(ctx)\n   180→\tdiags = diags.Append(checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(evalDiags))\n   181→\n   182→\tif wantType != cty.DynamicPseudoType {\n   183→\t\tvar convErr error\n   184→\t\tval, convErr = convert.Convert(val, wantType)\n   185→\t\tif convErr != nil {\n   186→\t\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(wantType)\n   187→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   188→\t\t\t\tSeverity:    hcl.DiagError,\n   189→\t\t\t\tSummary:     \"Incorrect value type\",\n   190→\t\t\t\tDetail:      fmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid expression value: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(convErr)),\n   191→\t\t\t\tSubject:     expr.Range().Ptr(),\n   192→\t\t\t\tExpression:  expr,\n   193→\t\t\t\tEvalContext: ctx,\n   194→\t\t\t})\n   195→\t\t}\n   196→\t}\n   197→\n   198→\treturn val, diags\n   199→}\n   200→\n   201→// EvalReference evaluates the given reference in the receiving scope and\n   202→// returns the resulting value. The value will be converted to the given type before\n   203→// it is returned if possible, or else an error diagnostic will be produced\n   204→// describing the conversion error.\n   205→//\n   206→// Pass an expected type of cty.DynamicPseudoType to skip automatic conversion\n   207→// and just obtain the returned value directly.\n   208→//\n   209→// If the returned diagnostics contains errors then the result may be\n   210→// incomplete, but will always be of the requested type.\n   211→func (s *Scope) EvalReference(ref *addrs.Reference, wantType cty.Type) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   212→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   213→\n   214→\t// We cheat a bit here and just build an EvalContext for our requested\n   215→\t// reference with the \"self\" address overridden, and then pull the \"self\"\n   216→\t// result out of it to return.\n   217→\tctx, ctxDiags := s.evalContext([]*addrs.Reference{ref}, ref.Subject)\n   218→\tdiags = diags.Append(ctxDiags)\n   219→\tval := ctx.Variables[\"self\"]\n   220→\tif val == cty.NilVal {\n   221→\t\tval = cty.DynamicVal\n   222→\t}\n   223→\n   224→\tvar convErr error\n   225→\tval, convErr = convert.Convert(val, wantType)\n   226→\tif convErr != nil {\n   227→\t\tval = cty.UnknownVal(wantType)\n   228→\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   229→\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   230→\t\t\tSummary:  \"Incorrect value type\",\n   231→\t\t\tDetail:   fmt.Sprintf(\"Invalid expression value: %s.\", tfdiags.FormatError(convErr)),\n   232→\t\t\tSubject:  ref.SourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   233→\t\t})\n   234→\t}\n   235→\n   236→\treturn val, diags\n   237→}\n   238→\n   239→// EvalContext constructs a HCL expression evaluation context whose variable\n   240→// scope contains sufficient values to satisfy the given set of references.\n   241→//\n   242→// Most callers should prefer to use the evaluation helper methods that\n   243→// this type offers, but this is here for less common situations where the\n   244→// caller will handle the evaluation calls itself.\n   245→func (s *Scope) EvalContext(refs []*addrs.Reference) (*hcl.EvalContext, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   246→\treturn s.evalContext(refs, s.SelfAddr)\n   247→}\n   248→\n   249→func (s *Scope) evalContext(refs []*addrs.Reference, selfAddr addrs.Referenceable) (*hcl.EvalContext, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   250→\tif s == nil {\n   251→\t\tpanic(\"attempt to construct EvalContext for nil Scope\")\n   252→\t}\n   253→\n   254→\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n   255→\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   256→\tfuncs := s.Functions()\n   257→\tctx := &hcl.EvalContext{\n   258→\t\tVariables: vals,\n   259→\t\tFunctions: funcs,\n   260→\t}\n   261→\n   262→\tif len(refs) == 0 {\n   263→\t\t// Easy path for common case where there are no references at all.\n   264→\t\treturn ctx, diags\n   265→\t}\n   266→\n   267→\t// First we'll do static validation of the references. This catches things\n   268→\t// early that might otherwise not get caught due to unknown values being\n   269→\t// present in the scope during planning.\n   270→\tstaticDiags := s.Data.StaticValidateReferences(refs, selfAddr, s.SourceAddr)\n   271→\tdiags = diags.Append(staticDiags)\n   272→\tif staticDiags.HasErrors() {\n   273→\t\treturn ctx, diags\n   274→\t}\n   275→\n   276→\t// The reference set we are given has not been de-duped, and so there can\n   277→\t// be redundant requests in it for two reasons:\n   278→\t//  - The same item is referenced multiple times\n   279→\t//  - Both an item and that item's container are separately referenced.\n   280→\t// We will still visit every reference here and ask our data source for\n   281→\t// it, since that allows us to gather a full set of any errors and\n   282→\t// warnings, but once we've gathered all the data we'll then skip anything\n   283→\t// that's redundant in the process of populating our values map.\n   284→\tdataResources := map[string]map[string]cty.Value{}\n   285→\tmanagedResources := map[string]map[string]cty.Value{}\n   286→\twholeModules := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   287→\tinputVariables := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   288→\tlocalValues := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   289→\toutputValues := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   290→\tpathAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   291→\tterraformAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   292→\tcountAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   293→\tforEachAttrs := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   294→\tcheckBlocks := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   295→\trunBlocks := map[string]cty.Value{}\n   296→\tvar self cty.Value\n   297→\n   298→\tfor _, ref := range refs {\n   299→\t\trng := ref.SourceRange\n   300→\n   301→\t\trawSubj := ref.Subject\n   302→\t\tif rawSubj == addrs.Self {\n   303→\t\t\tif selfAddr == nil {\n   304→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(&hcl.Diagnostic{\n   305→\t\t\t\t\tSeverity: hcl.DiagError,\n   306→\t\t\t\t\tSummary:  `Invalid \"self\" reference`,\n   307→\t\t\t\t\t// This detail message mentions some current practice that\n   308→\t\t\t\t\t// this codepath doesn't really \"know about\". If the \"self\"\n   309→\t\t\t\t\t// object starts being supported in more contexts later then\n   310→\t\t\t\t\t// we'll need to adjust this message.\n   311→\t\t\t\t\tDetail:  `The \"self\" object is not available in this context. This object can be used only in resource provisioner, connection, and postcondition blocks.`,\n   312→\t\t\t\t\tSubject: ref.SourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr(),\n   313→\t\t\t\t})\n   314→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   315→\t\t\t}\n   316→\n   317→\t\t\tif selfAddr == addrs.Self {\n   318→\t\t\t\t// Programming error: the self address cannot alias itself.\n   319→\t\t\t\tpanic(\"scope SelfAddr attempting to alias itself\")\n   320→\t\t\t}\n   321→\n   322→\t\t\t// self can only be used within a resource instance\n   323→\t\t\tsubj := selfAddr.(addrs.ResourceInstance)\n   324→\n   325→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetResource(subj.ContainingResource(), rng))\n   326→\n   327→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   328→\n   329→\t\t\t// Self is an exception in that it must always resolve to a\n   330→\t\t\t// particular instance. We will still insert the full resource into\n   331→\t\t\t// the context below.\n   332→\t\t\tvar hclDiags hcl.Diagnostics\n   333→\t\t\t// We should always have a valid self index by this point, but in\n   334→\t\t\t// the case of an error, self may end up as a cty.DynamicValue.\n   335→\t\t\tswitch k := subj.Key.(type) {\n   336→\t\t\tcase addrs.IntKey:\n   337→\t\t\t\tself, hclDiags = hcl.Index(val, cty.NumberIntVal(int64(k)), ref.SourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr())\n   338→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(hclDiags)\n   339→\t\t\tcase addrs.StringKey:\n   340→\t\t\t\tself, hclDiags = hcl.Index(val, cty.StringVal(string(k)), ref.SourceRange.ToHCL().Ptr())\n   341→\t\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(hclDiags)\n   342→\t\t\tdefault:\n   343→\t\t\t\tself = val\n   344→\t\t\t}\n   345→\t\t\tcontinue\n   346→\t\t}\n   347→\n   348→\t\t// This type switch must cover all of the \"Referenceable\" implementations\n   349→\t\t// in package addrs, however we are removing the possibility of\n   350→\t\t// Instances beforehand.\n   351→\t\tswitch addr := rawSubj.(type) {\n   352→\t\tcase addrs.ResourceInstance:\n   353→\t\t\trawSubj = addr.ContainingResource()\n   354→\t\tcase addrs.ModuleCallInstance:\n   355→\t\t\trawSubj = addr.Call\n   356→\t\tcase addrs.ModuleCallInstanceOutput:\n   357→\t\t\trawSubj = addr.Call.Call\n   358→\t\t}\n   359→\n   360→\t\tswitch subj := rawSubj.(type) {\n   361→\t\tcase addrs.Resource:\n   362→\t\t\tvar into map[string]map[string]cty.Value\n   363→\t\t\tswitch subj.Mode {\n   364→\t\t\tcase addrs.ManagedResourceMode:\n   365→\t\t\t\tinto = managedResources\n   366→\t\t\tcase addrs.DataResourceMode:\n   367→\t\t\t\tinto = dataResources\n   368→\t\t\tdefault:\n   369→\t\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported ResourceMode %s\", subj.Mode))\n   370→\t\t\t}\n   371→\n   372→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetResource(subj, rng))\n   373→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   374→\n   375→\t\t\tr := subj\n   376→\t\t\tif into[r.Type] == nil {\n   377→\t\t\t\tinto[r.Type] = make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   378→\t\t\t}\n   379→\t\t\tinto[r.Type][r.Name] = val\n   380→\n   381→\t\tcase addrs.ModuleCall:\n   382→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetModule(subj, rng))\n   383→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   384→\t\t\twholeModules[subj.Name] = val\n   385→\n   386→\t\tcase addrs.InputVariable:\n   387→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetInputVariable(subj, rng))\n   388→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   389→\t\t\tinputVariables[subj.Name] = val\n   390→\n   391→\t\tcase addrs.LocalValue:\n   392→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetLocalValue(subj, rng))\n   393→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   394→\t\t\tlocalValues[subj.Name] = val\n   395→\n   396→\t\tcase addrs.PathAttr:\n   397→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetPathAttr(subj, rng))\n   398→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   399→\t\t\tpathAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   400→\n   401→\t\tcase addrs.TerraformAttr:\n   402→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetTerraformAttr(subj, rng))\n   403→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   404→\t\t\tterraformAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   405→\n   406→\t\tcase addrs.CountAttr:\n   407→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetCountAttr(subj, rng))\n   408→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   409→\t\t\tcountAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   410→\n   411→\t\tcase addrs.ForEachAttr:\n   412→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetForEachAttr(subj, rng))\n   413→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   414→\t\t\tforEachAttrs[subj.Name] = val\n   415→\n   416→\t\tcase addrs.OutputValue:\n   417→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetOutput(subj, rng))\n   418→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   419→\t\t\toutputValues[subj.Name] = val\n   420→\n   421→\t\tcase addrs.Check:\n   422→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetCheckBlock(subj, rng))\n   423→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   424→\t\t\tcheckBlocks[subj.Name] = val\n   425→\n   426→\t\tcase addrs.Run:\n   427→\t\t\tval, valDiags := normalizeRefValue(s.Data.GetRunBlock(subj, rng))\n   428→\t\t\tdiags = diags.Append(valDiags)\n   429→\t\t\trunBlocks[subj.Name] = val\n   430→\n   431→\t\tdefault:\n   432→\t\t\t// Should never happen\n   433→\t\t\tpanic(fmt.Errorf(\"Scope.buildEvalContext cannot handle address type %T\", rawSubj))\n   434→\t\t}\n   435→\t}\n   436→\n   437→\t// Managed resources are exposed in two different locations. The primary\n   438→\t// is at the top level where the resource type name is the root of the\n   439→\t// traversal, but we also expose them under \"resource\" as an escaping\n   440→\t// technique if we add a reserved name in a future language edition which\n   441→\t// conflicts with someone's existing provider.\n   442→\tfor k, v := range buildResourceObjects(managedResources) {\n   443→\t\tvals[k] = v\n   444→\t}\n   445→\tvals[\"resource\"] = cty.ObjectVal(buildResourceObjects(managedResources))\n   446→\n   447→\tvals[\"data\"] = cty.ObjectVal(buildResourceObjects(dataResources))\n   448→\tvals[\"module\"] = cty.ObjectVal(wholeModules)\n   449→\tvals[\"var\"] = cty.ObjectVal(inputVariables)\n   450→\tvals[\"local\"] = cty.ObjectVal(localValues)\n   451→\tvals[\"path\"] = cty.ObjectVal(pathAttrs)\n   452→\tvals[\"terraform\"] = cty.ObjectVal(terraformAttrs)\n   453→\tvals[\"count\"] = cty.ObjectVal(countAttrs)\n   454→\tvals[\"each\"] = cty.ObjectVal(forEachAttrs)\n   455→\n   456→\t// Checks, outputs, and run blocks are conditionally included in the\n   457→\t// available scope, so we'll only write out their values if we actually have\n   458→\t// something for them.\n   459→\tif len(checkBlocks) > 0 {\n   460→\t\tvals[\"check\"] = cty.ObjectVal(checkBlocks)\n   461→\t}\n   462→\n   463→\tif len(outputValues) > 0 {\n   464→\t\tvals[\"output\"] = cty.ObjectVal(outputValues)\n   465→\t}\n   466→\n   467→\tif len(runBlocks) > 0 {\n   468→\t\tvals[\"run\"] = cty.ObjectVal(runBlocks)\n   469→\t}\n   470→\n   471→\tif self != cty.NilVal {\n   472→\t\tvals[\"self\"] = self\n   473→\t}\n   474→\n   475→\treturn ctx, diags\n   476→}\n   477→\n   478→func buildResourceObjects(resources map[string]map[string]cty.Value) map[string]cty.Value {\n   479→\tvals := make(map[string]cty.Value)\n   480→\tfor typeName, nameVals := range resources {\n   481→\t\tvals[typeName] = cty.ObjectVal(nameVals)\n   482→\t}\n   483→\treturn vals\n   484→}\n   485→\n   486→func normalizeRefValue(val cty.Value, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   487→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   488→\t\t// If there are errors then we will force an unknown result so that\n   489→\t\t// we can still evaluate and catch type errors but we'll avoid\n   490→\t\t// producing redundant re-statements of the same errors we've already\n   491→\t\t// dealt with here.\n   492→\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(val.Type()), diags\n   493→\t}\n   494→\treturn val, diags\n   495→}\n   496→\n   497→// checkForUnknownFunctionDiags inspects the diagnostics for errors from unknown\n   498→// function calls, and tailors the messages to better suit Terraform. We now\n   499→// have multiple namespaces where functions may be declared, and it's up to the\n   500→// user to have properly configured the module to populate the provider\n   501→// namespace. The generic unknown function diagnostic from hcl does not direct\n   502→// the user on how to remedy the situation in Terraform, and we can give more\n   503→// useful information in a few Terraform specific cases here.\n   504→func checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(diags hcl.Diagnostics) hcl.Diagnostics {\n   505→\tfor _, d := range diags {\n   506→\t\textra, ok := hcl.DiagnosticExtra[hclsyntax.FunctionCallUnknownDiagExtra](d)\n   507→\t\tif !ok {\n   508→\t\t\tcontinue\n   509→\t\t}\n   510→\t\tname := extra.CalledFunctionName()\n   511→\t\tnamespace := extra.CalledFunctionNamespace()\n   512→\t\tnamespaceParts := strings.Split(namespace, \"::\")\n   513→\t\tif len(namespaceParts) < 2 {\n   514→\t\t\t// no namespace (namespace includes ::, so will have at least 2\n   515→\t\t\t// parts), but check if there is a matching name in a provider\n   516→\t\t\t// namspace.\n   517→\t\t\tif d.EvalContext == nil {\n   518→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   519→\t\t\t}\n   520→\n   521→\t\t\tfor funcName := range d.EvalContext.Functions {\n   522→\t\t\t\tif strings.HasSuffix(funcName, \"::\"+name) {\n   523→\t\t\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(\"%s Did you mean %q?\", d.Detail, funcName)\n   524→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   525→\t\t\t\t}\n   526→\t\t\t}\n   527→\t\t\tcontinue\n   528→\t\t}\n   529→\n   530→\t\t// the diagnostic isn't really shared with anything, and copying would\n   531→\t\t// still retain the internal pointers, so we're going to modify the\n   532→\t\t// diagnostic in-place if we want to change the output. Log the original\n   533→\t\t// diagnostic for debugging purposes in case we overwrite something\n   534→\t\t// potentially useful in the future from hcl.\n   535→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] UnknownFunctionCall: %s\", d.Error())\n   536→\t\td.Summary = \"Unknown provider function\"\n   537→\n   538→\t\tif namespaceParts[0] != \"provider\" {\n   539→\t\t\t// help if the user is skipping the provider:: prefix before the\n   540→\t\t\t// provider name.\n   541→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`The function namespace %q is not valid. Provider function calls must use the \"provider::\" namespace prefix.`, namespaceParts[0])\n   542→\t\t\tcontinue\n   543→\t\t}\n   544→\n   545→\t\tif namespaceParts[1] == \"\" {\n   546→\t\t\t// missing provider name entirely\n   547→\t\t\td.Detail = `The function call must include the provider name after the \"provider::\" prefix.`\n   548→\t\t\tcontinue\n   549→\t\t}\n   550→\n   551→\t\tif d.EvalContext == nil {\n   552→\t\t\t// There's no eval context for some reason, so we can't inspect the\n   553→\t\t\t// available functions.\n   554→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`There is no function named \"%s%s\".`, namespace, name)\n   555→\t\t\tcontinue\n   556→\t\t}\n   557→\n   558→\t\totherProviderFuncs := false\n   559→\t\tfor funcName := range d.EvalContext.Functions {\n   560→\t\t\t// there are other functions in this provider namespace, so it must\n   561→\t\t\t// have been included in the configuration, and we can be clear that\n   562→\t\t\t// this a function which the provider does not support.\n   563→\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(funcName, namespace) {\n   564→\t\t\t\totherProviderFuncs = true\n   565→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   566→\t\t\t}\n   567→\t\t}\n   568→\t\tif otherProviderFuncs {\n   569→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(\"The function %q is not available from the provider %q.\", name, namespaceParts[1])\n   570→\t\t\tcontinue\n   571→\t\t}\n   572→\n   573→\t\t// no other functions exist for this provider, so hint that the user may\n   574→\t\t// need to include it in the configuration.\n   575→\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`There is no function named \"%s%s\". Ensure that provider name %q is declared in this module's required_providers block, and that this provider offers a function named %q.`, namespace, name, namespaceParts[1], name)\n   576→\t}\n   577→\n   578→\treturn diags\n   579→}\n   580→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. 483→\tfor typeName, nameVals := range resources {\n   484→\t\tvals[typeName] = cty.ObjectVal(nameVals)\n   485→\t}\n   486→\treturn vals\n   487→}\n   488→\n   489→func normalizeRefValue(val cty.Value, diags tfdiags.Diagnostics) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n   490→\tif diags.HasErrors() {\n   491→\t\t// If there are errors then we will force an unknown result so that\n   492→\t\t// function calls, and tailors the messages to better suit Terraform. We now\n   502→// have multiple namespaces where functions may be declared, and it's up to the\n   503→// user to have properly configured the module to populate the provider\n   504→// namespace. The generic unknown function diagnostic from hcl does not direct\n   505→// the user on how to remedy the situation in Terraform, and we can give more\n   506→// useful information in a few Terraform specific cases here.\n   507→func checkForUnknownFunctionDiags(diags hcl.Diagnostics) hcl.Diagnostics {\n   508→\tfor _, d := range diags {\n   509→\t\textra, ok := hcl.DiagnosticExtra[hclsyntax.FunctionCallUnknownDiagExtra](d)\n   510→\t\tif !ok {\n   511→\t\t\tcontinue\n   512→\t\t}\n   513→\t\tname := extra.CalledFunctionName()\n   514→\t\tnamespace := extra.CalledFunctionNamespace()\n   515→\t\tnamespaceParts := strings.Split(namespace, \"::\")\n   516→\t\tif len(namespaceParts) < 2 {\n   517→\t\t\t// no namespace (namespace includes ::, so will have at least 2\n   518→\t\t\t// parts), but check if there is a matching name in a provider\n   519→\t\t\t// namspace.\n   520→\t\t\tif d.EvalContext == nil {\n   521→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   522→\t\t\t}\n   523→\n   524→\t\t\tfor funcName := range d.EvalContext.Functions {\n   525→\t\t\t\tif strings.HasSuffix(funcName, \"::\"+name) {\n   526→\t\t\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(\"%s Did you mean %q?\", d.Detail, funcName)\n   527→\t\t\t\t\tbreak\n   528→\t\t\t\t}\n   529→\t\t\t}\n   530→\t\t\tcontinue\n   531→\t\t}\n   532→\n   533→\t\t// the diagnostic isn't really shared with anything, and copying would\n   534→\t\t// still retain the internal pointers, so we're going to modify the\n   535→\t\t// diagnostic in-place if we want to change the output. Log the original\n   536→\t\t// diagnostic for debugging purposes in case we overwrite something\n   537→\t\t// potentially useful in the future from hcl.\n   538→\t\tlog.Printf(\"[ERROR] UnknownFunctionCall: %s\", d.Error())\n   539→\t\td.Summary = \"Unknown provider function\"\n   540→\n   541→\t\tif namespaceParts[0] != \"provider\" {\n   542→\t\t\t// help if the user is skipping the provider:: prefix before the\n   543→\t\t\t// provider name.\n   544→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`The function namespace %q is not valid. Provider function calls must use the \"provider::\" namespace prefix.`, namespaceParts[0])\n   545→\t\t\tcontinue\n   546→\t\t}\n   547→\n   548→\t\tif namespaceParts[1] == \"\" {\n   549→\t\t\t// missing provider name entirely\n   550→\t\t\td.Detail = `The function call must include the provider name after the \"provider::\" prefix.`\n   551→\t\t\tcontinue\n   552→\t\t}\n   553→\n   554→\t\tif d.EvalContext == nil {\n   555→\t\t\t// There's no eval context for some reason, so we can't inspect the\n   556→\t\t\t// available functions.\n   557→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`There is no function named \"%s%s\".`, namespace, name)\n   558→\t\t\tcontinue\n   559→\t\t}\n   560→\n   561→\t\totherProviderFuncs := false\n   562→\t\tfor funcName := range d.EvalContext.Functions {\n   563→\t\t\t// there are other functions in this provider namespace, so it must\n   564→\t\t\t// have been included in the configuration, and we can be clear that\n   565→\t\t\t// this a function which the provider does not support.\n   566→\t\t\tif strings.HasPrefix(funcName, namespace) {\n   567→\t\t\t\totherProviderFuncs = true\n   568→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   569→\t\t\t}\n   570→\t\t}\n   571→\t\tif otherProviderFuncs {\n   572→\t\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(\"The function %q is not available from the provider %q.\", name, namespaceParts[1])\n   573→\t\t\tcontinue\n   574→\t\t}\n   575→\n   576→\t\t// no other functions exist for this provider, so hint that the user may\n   577→\t\t// need to include it in the configuration.\n   578→\t\td.Detail = fmt.Sprintf(`There is no function named \"%s%s\". Ensure that provider name %q is declared in this module's required_providers block, and that this provider offers a function named %q.`, namespace, name, namespaceParts[1], name)\n   579→\t}\n   580→\n   581→\treturn diags\n   582→}\n   583→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. 53→\t\t},\n    54→\t}\n    55→\n    56→\tfor _, test := range tests {\n    57→\t\tt.Run(fmt.Sprintf(\"sensitive(%#v)\", test.Input), func(t *testing.T) {\n    58→\t\t\tgot, err := nil {\n    69→\t\t\t\tt.Fatalf(\"unexpected error: %s\", err)\n    70→\t\t\t}\n    71→\n    72→\t\t\tif !got.HasMark(marks.Sensitive) {\n    73→\t\t\t\tt.Errorf(\"result is not marked sensitive\")\n    74→\t\t\t}\n    75→\n    76→\t\t\tgotRaw, _ := got.Unmark()\n    77→\n    78→\t\t\t// Disregarding shallow marks, the result should have the same\n    79→\t\t\t// effective value as the input.\n    80→\t\t\twantRaw, _ := test.Input.Unmark()\n    81→\t\t\tif !gotRaw.RawEquals(wantRaw) {\n    82→\t\t\t\tt.Errorf(\"wrong unmarked result\\ngot:  %#v\\nwant: %#v\", got, wantRaw)\n    83→\t\t\t}\n    84→\t\t})\n    85→\t}\n    86→}\n    87→\n    88→func TestNonsensitive(t *testing.T) {\n    89→\ttests := []struct {\n    90→\t\tInput   cty.Value\n    91→\t\tWantErr string\n    92→\t}{\n versions 1.9.0 and 1.10.0, here are the key changes related to how conditional expressions handle sensitive marks propagation:\n\n### 1. **Sensitive Function Implementation Changes**\n\n**File:** `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/internal/lang/funcs/sensitive.go` → `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/funcs/sensitive.go`\n\n**Changes in `SensitiveFunc`:**\n- **v1.9.0**: Unmarked the input value before marking it as sensitive\n  ```go\n  Impl: func(args []cty.Value, retType cty.Type) (ret cty.Value, err error) {\n      val, _ := args[0].Unmark()\n      return val.Mark(marks.Sensitive), nil\n  }\n  ```\n- **v1.10.0**: Now directly marks the input value without unmarking\n  ```go\n  Impl: func(args []cty.Value, retType cty.Type) (ret cty.Value, err error) {\n      return args[0].Mark(marks.Sensitive), nil\n  }\n  ```\n  This preserves any existing marks on the value.\n\n**Changes in `IssensitiveFunc`:**\n- **v1.9.0**: Simply checked if the value had the sensitive mark\n  ```go\n  Impl: func(args []cty.Value, retType cty.Type) (cty.Value, error) {\n      s := args[0].HasMark(marks.Sensitive)\n      return cty.BoolVal(s), nil\n  }\n  ```\n- **v1.10.0**: Now returns `UnknownVal` for unknown inputs to match the plan/apply consistency issue (#36012)\n  ```go\n  Impl: func(args []cty.Value, retType cty.Type) (cty.Value, error) {\n      switch v := args[0]; {\n      case v.HasMark(marks.Sensitive):\n          return cty.True, nil\n      case !v.IsKnown():\n          return cty.UnknownVal(cty.Bool), nil\n      default:\n          return cty.False, nil\n      }\n  }\n  ```\n\n### 2. **Type Conversion Function Changes**\n\n**File:** `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/internal/lang/funcs/conversion.go` → `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/funcs/conversion.go`\n\n**Changes in `MakeToFunc` (for `tostring()`, `tonumber()`, `tobool()`, etc.):**\n- **v1.9.0**: Assumed the input was always known (no unknown handling)\n- **v1.10.0**: Added `AllowUnknown: true` and now propagates marks to unknown values using `WithSameMarks()`\n  ```go\n  if !args[0].IsKnown() {\n      return cty.UnknownVal(retType).WithSameMarks(args[0]), nil\n  }\n  ```\n  This ensures marks (like sensitive and ephemeral) are preserved when converting unknown values.\n\n### 3. **New Ephemeral Mark Support**\n\n**New Files in v1.10.0:**\n- `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/ephemeral/doc.go`\n- `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/ephemeral/paths.go`\n\n**New Function:** `ephemeralasnull()` in `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/funcs/conversion.go`\n- Replaces ephemeral-marked values with non-ephemeral null values\n- Preserves non-ephemeral marks\n\n### 4. **Enhanced Mark Path Handling**\n\n**File:** `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/internal/lang/marks/paths.go` → `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/marks/paths.go`\n\n**New function added in v1.10.0:** `MarksEqual()`\n- Compares two unordered sets of `PathValueMarks` for equality\n- Uses sorted comparison for consistent results\n\n### 5. **Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions**\n\n**Issue Fixed:** #36017 - \"The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values\"\n\n**Key Changes:**\n- Marks must be combined from all values within a conditional expression to avoid losing mark information\n- This affects both `condition ? true_branch : false_branch` ternary expressions and `for` expressions\n- The fix ensures that marks are properly propagated even when one branch contains unknown values\n\n**CHANGELOG Entry:**\n- \"config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\"\n\n### 6. **Test Changes**\n\n**File:** `/workspace/terraform-v1.9.0/internal/lang/funcs/sensitive_test.go` → `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/funcs/sensitive_test.go`\n\nChanges to the test suite:\n- Removed test case for non-standard marks being \"fixed\" to sensitive mark\n- Updated `IssensitiveFunc` test to handle unknown values returning unknown boolean\n- Changed test assertions to use `RawEquals()` for comparing results\n\n### 7. **Supporting Changes in Other Functions**\n\n**New Ephemeral-aware code in v1.10.0:**\n- `/workspace/terraform-v1.10.0/internal/lang/funcs/filesystem.go`: Added handling for ephemeral marks\n- Enhanced mark handling in conversion functions to use `WithSameMarks()` and `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`\n\n## Key Takeaway\n\nThe primary change is that **Terraform v1.10.0 now properly propagates marks (sensitive and ephemeral) through conditional expressions and type conversions**, whereas v1.9.0 could lose these marks in certain combinations with unknown values. This is achieved by:\n\n1. Using `WithSameMarks()` to preserve marks during conversions\n2. Modifying the `sensitive()` function to preserve existing marks instead of stripping them\n3. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014ELRqX9fjujGEWsArYjaJm","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01M2t9ybwfWFXYzc2HCngHjR","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces significant improvements to backend configuration, resource addressing, sensitive value handling, and introduces a new ephemeral resources feature. This guide covers the breaking changes and migration steps required to upgrade from v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.\n\n**Key themes:**\n- S3 backend configuration simplification with new `assume_role` block syntax\n- Enhanced `moved` block functionality requiring explicit resource type qualification for reserved keywords\n- Improved sensitive value propagation in conditional expressions\n- Introduction of ephemeral input variables, outputs, and resources for secure secret handling\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend IAM Role Assumption Attributes Deprecated\n\n#### What Changed\n\nThe S3 backend in v1.9.0 used individual attributes for IAM role assumption:\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\nAll these attributes are **deprecated as of v1.10.0** and will be removed in a future version. They are replaced by the new `assume_role` nested block.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe `assume_role` block provides:\n- Better schema organization and validation\n- Support for new features like `source_identity`\n- Consistent with other AWS provider block patterns\n- Clearer intent through block structure rather than prefixed attributes\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                          = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                             = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                          = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn                        = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                    = \"terraform\"\n    external_id                     = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds    = 3600\n    assume_role_policy              = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Purpose = \"Terraform\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      duration    = \"1h\"\n      external_id = \"unique-external-id\"\n      policy      = jsonencode({...})\n\n      tags = {\n        Purpose = \"Terraform\"\n      }\n\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Purpose\"]\n\n      # New in v1.10.0: Specify source identity for the assumed role\n      source_identity = \"terraform-automation\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify all S3 backends using the deprecated attributes:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"role_arn\\|session_name\\|external_id\\|assume_role_duration\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update your backend configuration:**\n   - Replace individual `assume_role_*` attributes with the `assume_role` block\n   - Convert `assume_role_duration_seconds` to `duration` using time duration format (e.g., \"3600s\" or \"1h\")\n   - Note: `session_name` is now `session_name` within the block (attribute name unchanged)\n   - `assume_role_policy` becomes `policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` becomes `policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` becomes `tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` becomes `transitive_tag_keys`\n\n3. **Test the new configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -upgrade\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration Format:** The new `duration` attribute requires string values in time format. Use \"1h\", \"30m\", or \"3600s\" instead of seconds as a number.\n- **Missing scope:** If you have other IAM settings, ensure they're still included (e.g., `access_key`, `secret_key`, or AWS credential chain)\n- **Validation changes:** The `assume_role` block has stricter validation. All ARNs must follow proper AWS ARN format.\n\n#### Deprecation Timeline\n\n- v1.10.0: Deprecated (still works with deprecation warnings)\n- Future version: Will be removed entirely\n\n---\n\n### 2. New S3 Native State Locking Support (Experimental)\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces experimental support for S3-native state locking without requiring DynamoDB. This is controlled by the new `use_lockfile` attribute.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Required for state locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Option 1: Keep DynamoDB\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Option 2: Use S3 Native Locking (Experimental)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket        = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key           = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region        = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile  = true  # Enable S3-native locking\n    # Note: omit dynamodb_table when using use_lockfile\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\nTo migrate from DynamoDB to S3 native locking:\n\n1. **Enable `use_lockfile` in your backend configuration:**\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       use_lockfile = true\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Test with `terraform plan` first** (doesn't acquire state lock):\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n3. **Perform a state refresh** to verify locking works:\n   ```bash\n   terraform refresh\n   ```\n\n4. **Once verified, you can optionally remove the DynamoDB reference:**\n   - Remove `dynamodb_table` attribute\n   - Delete the DynamoDB table if no longer needed\n\n#### Compatibility Notes\n\n- **Experimental Status:** This feature is marked as experimental and may change in future releases\n- **Backwards Compatibility:** If both `dynamodb_table` and `use_lockfile` are specified, `dynamodb_table` takes precedence\n- **Permissions:** Requires `s3:GetObject`, `s3:PutObject`, and `s3:DeleteObject` permissions on the state file object\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks Now Require \"resource.\" Prefix for Reserved Keywords\n\n#### What Changed\n\nWhen using `moved` blocks to refactor resource locations, if your resource type name matches a top-level Terraform keyword (like `resource`, `module`, `data`, `variable`, `local`, etc.), you must now explicitly prepend `resource.` to disambiguate it.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nWithout the explicit prefix, Terraform couldn't distinguish between:\n- A resource with type name \"module\" (e.g., `resource \"module\" \"example\"`)\n- A reference to a module (e.g., `module.example`)\n\nThe `resource.` prefix makes the intent unambiguous.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = module.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n\n# This was ambiguous for resource types matching keywords:\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_name      # Is this a local variable or a resource?\n  to   = custom_module.new   # Is this a module or a resource?\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nFor resources with type names matching reserved keywords, prepend `resource.`:\n\n```hcl\n# Moving a resource type named \"local\" - must use resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n\n# Moving a resource type named \"module\" - must use resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.module.old_instance\n  to   = resource.module.new_instance\n}\n\n# Regular moves (non-keyword resource types) still work without prefix\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old\n  to   = aws_instance.new\n}\n\n# Module moves always use the \"module\" keyword (not resource.module)\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module\n  to   = module.new_module\n}\n```\n\n#### Reserved Keywords Requiring \"resource.\" Prefix\n\nThe following keywords require the `resource.` prefix when used as resource type names:\n\n- `resource`\n- `data`\n- `module`\n- `variable`\n- `local`\n- `output`\n- `terraform`\n- `provider`\n- `moved`\n- `removed`\n- `import`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify moved blocks that reference reserved keywords:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -A 1 \"moved {\" *.tf | grep -E \"from|to.*\\s+(local|module|data|resource|variable|output|path|self|count|each|terraform|provider|template|lazy|arg)\\.\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update the affected moved blocks:**\n   - If the resource type name is a reserved keyword, add `resource.` prefix to both `from` and `to` addresses\n   - Examples:\n     ```hcl\n     # Before\n     moved {\n       from = local.example\n       to   = local.moved_example\n     }\n\n     # After\n     moved {\n       from = resource.local.example\n       to   = resource.local.moved_example\n     }\n     ```\n\n3. **Verify the configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Module moves don't need \"resource.\":** Moving modules still uses `module.old_module` syntax, not `resource.module.old_module`\n- **Data sources don't use \"resource.\":** Data sources use `data.type.name` syntax naturally\n- **Only for resource type names:** The prefix is only needed when the resource *type* matches a keyword, not when moving from non-keyword types\n\n#### Error Message Example\n\nIf you forget to use `resource.` prefix:\n\n```\nError: Invalid \"moved\" addresses\n\nThe keyword \"local\" is reserved and cannot be used to target a resource\naddress. If you are targeting a resource type that uses a reserved keyword,\nplease prefix your address with \"resource.\".\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, sensitive marks could be lost when values flowed through conditional (ternary) expressions. In v1.10.0, sensitive marks are properly propagated through all branches of conditional expressions, even when branches contain unknown values.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nTo prevent accidental exposure of sensitive values and to ensure consistent behavior between plan and apply phases.\n\n**Related Issue:** #36017\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0) - Marks Could Be Lost\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"prod\"\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0, the sensitive mark could be lost in this conditional\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.database_password : \"default-password\"\n  description = \"This might NOT be marked sensitive due to the conditional!\"\n}\n```\n\nIn v1.9.0, if one branch was unknown, Terraform might lose the sensitive mark from the other branch.\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Marks Are Always Preserved\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"prod\"\n}\n\n# In v1.10.0, the sensitive mark is properly preserved\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.database_password : \"default-password\"\n  description = \"This is now correctly marked sensitive!\"\n}\n```\n\nThe output `db_password` is correctly marked as sensitive, even though one branch is a literal string.\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review conditional expressions that work with sensitive values:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"?\\|:\" *.tf | grep -i \"password\\|secret\\|key\\|token\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update `sensitive()` function usage if needed:**\n\n   In v1.9.0, you might have worked around mark loss:\n   ```hcl\n   # v1.9.0 workaround (no longer needed)\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = sensitive(var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.secret : \"fallback\")\n   }\n   ```\n\n   In v1.10.0, this is still valid but unnecessary:\n   ```hcl\n   # v1.10.0 - marks now propagate automatically\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.secret : \"fallback\"\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Update logic using `issensitive()` function:**\n\n   In v1.9.0:\n   ```hcl\n   if issensitive(my_var) {\n     # Assume it's definitely sensitive\n   }\n   ```\n\n   In v1.10.0, `issensitive()` returns `unknown` for unknown values:\n   ```hcl\n   # Update your logic to handle unknown results\n   value = issensitive(my_var)\n   # value could now be true, false, or unknown\n   ```\n\n4. **Handle ephemeral values in conditionals:**\n\n   New in v1.10.0 - use `ephemeralasnull()` to replace ephemeral values:\n   ```hcl\n   # Replace ephemeral values with non-ephemeral nulls for persistence\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = ephemeralasnull(var.ephemeral_secret)\n  }\n   ```\n\n#### Impact on Plan Output\n\nWith improved mark propagation, Terraform state files may now show more values as sensitive than before. This is more correct behavior. For example:\n\n```diff\n# Before (v1.9.0)\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value = \"MyPassword123\"  # Not marked sensitive (mark was lost)\n}\n\n# After (v1.10.0)\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value = \"***\"  # Correctly marked sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **`issensitive()` behavior change:** It now returns unknown for unknown inputs instead of false. Update any conditional logic that depends on this function.\n- **Type conversion functions:** Functions like `tostring()`, `tonumber()`, `tobool()` now preserve marks through conversions\n- **`nonsensitive()` function:** Use this explicitly if you need to remove the sensitive mark\n  ```hcl\n  output \"raw_password\" {\n    value = nonsensitive(var.database_password)\n  }\n  ```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 5. Ephemeral Input Variables and Outputs\n\n#### What Is It?\n\nEphemeral values are a new category in Terraform that exist only in memory during a single Terraform phase (plan or apply) and are never persisted to state files, plans, or outputs. This is useful for short-lived secrets, tokens, or credentials that should not appear in any artifacts.\n\n#### Usage\n\n**Ephemeral Input Variables:**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  sensitive = true\n}\n```\n\n**Ephemeral Outputs:**\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = local_sensitive_data.credentials\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n}\n```\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n- **Not persisted:** Never written to state, plan files, or saved outputs\n- **Single phase only:** Values are discarded after the current phase (plan or apply) completes\n- **Use in provider configs:** Primarily intended for provider configurations and provisioners\n- **Cannot be referenced by non-ephemeral outputs:** Ephemeral values cannot flow into persistent outputs\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nIf you have sensitive values that should never persist:\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  # Still gets written to state file\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  ephemeral = true\n  # Never gets written to state file\n}\n```\n\n#### When to Use Ephemeral\n\nUse ephemeral for:\n- API tokens that expire quickly\n- Temporary credentials from STS AssumeRole\n- One-time passwords or codes\n- Session tokens\n\nDo NOT use ephemeral for:\n- Database passwords (need persistence for apply)\n- SSH keys (need persistence)\n- Regular sensitive data (use `sensitive = true`)\n\n#### Example: Ephemeral Variables with Assume Role\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. Ephemeral Resources\n\n#### What Is It?\n\nEphemeral resources are a new resource mode for opening short-lived connections or sessions. Unlike managed resources (which are created and stored in state), ephemeral resources:\n- Exist only during the current Terraform phase\n- Don't persist to state\n- Are automatically closed when the phase completes\n- Support renewal if their expiration time is approached\n\n#### Usage\n\nEphemeral resources are used in provider plugins and are less commonly used directly in configuration, but you might see them referenced in provider documentation:\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_assume_role_session\" \"provider_auth\" {\n  role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/ProviderRole\"\n  session_name = \"terraform-provider\"\n  duration_seconds = 900\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  # Use ephemeral credentials from the assumed role\n  assume_role {\n    role_arn = ephemeral.aws_assume_role_session.provider_auth.role_arn\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\n- **For most users:** No direct migration needed\n- **For provider developers:** May need to implement ephemeral resource support\n- **Existing configurations:** Not affected unless explicitly using ephemeral resources\n\n#### Key Features\n\n- **Automatic cleanup:** Closed automatically after phase completion\n- **Renewal support:** Providers can request renewal before expiration\n- **Prevents state explosion:** Temporary resources don't clutter the state file\n- **Secret protection:** Credentials don't persist in any artifacts\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Testing\n\n1. **Run validation on current configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan -out=backup.plan\n   ```\n\n2. **Check for deprecated patterns:**\n   ```bash\n   # Look for S3 backend IAM attributes\n   grep -r \"assume_role_\\|role_arn.*backend\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n\n   # Look for moved blocks with reserved keywords\n   grep -B 1 -A 1 \"moved.*local\\.\\|moved.*module\\.\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Review sensitive variable usage:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform console\n\n   # Try accessing sensitive outputs\n   > output.my_output  # Should show ***\n   ```\n\n### Migration Checklist\n\n- [ ] Backup current state file\n- [ ] Update S3 backend configuration if using deprecated IAM attributes\n- [ ] Update `moved` blocks to use `resource.` prefix for reserved keywords\n- [ ] Test the upgraded backend configuration\n- [ ] Review sensitive value handling in conditionals\n- [ ] Plan changes after upgrade\n- [ ] Apply changes with no resource modifications expected\n- [ ] Verify state file integrity\n- [ ] Test rollback procedures\n\n### Testing Commands\n\n```bash\n# Initialize with new backend (test connection)\nterraform init -upgrade\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Generate plan (should have no changes)\nterraform plan -detailed-exitcode\n# Expected: exit code 0 (no changes)\n\n# Review state integrity\nterraform show\n\n# List all resources to verify they're intact\nterraform state list\n```\n\n### Validation Testing\n\nTest that sensitive marks are preserved:\n\n```hcl\n# test.tf\nvariable \"secret_value\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  default   = \"my-secret\"\n}\n\nvariable \"use_default\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = true\n}\n\noutput \"test_mark\" {\n  value       = var.use_default ? var.secret_value : \"fallback\"\n  description = \"Should be marked sensitive\"\n}\n\noutput \"check_mark\" {\n  value = issensitive(var.secret_value)\n}\n```\n\n```bash\nterraform init\nterraform apply\nterraform show  # Verify output shows \"***\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Migration Fails\n\n1. **Restore from backup:**\n   ```bash\n   # If you have a backup of terraform.tfstate\n   cp terraform.tfstate.backup terraform.tfstate\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes:**\n   ```bash\n   git checkout HEAD -- .  # If using git\n   ```\n\n3. **Downgrade Terraform version:**\n   ```bash\n   # If necessary, downgrade back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version\n\n   # Remove v1.10.0 binary and reinstall v1.9.0\n   # Process depends on your installation method\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify state consistency:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n### Reverting S3 Backend Changes\n\nIf you need to revert the `assume_role` block back to individual attributes:\n\n```hcl\n# Current (v1.10.0) - assume_role block\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-state\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      duration    = \"1h\"\n      external_id = \"my-external-id\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n# Revert to (v1.9.0) - individual attributes\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                       = \"my-state\"\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform\"\n    external_id                  = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n  }\n}\n\n# Then reinitialize\nterraform init\n```\n\n### Reverting Moved Block Changes\n\nIf you need to revert `moved` blocks with `resource.` prefix:\n\n```hcl\n# Current (v1.10.0) - with resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_value\n  to   = resource.local.new_value\n}\n\n# Simply remove the resource. prefix to revert\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_value\n  to   = local.new_value\n}\n```\n\nNote: After reverting, these will produce errors until you downgrade to v1.9.0.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n| Feature | v1.9.0 | v1.10.0 | Migration |\n|---------|--------|---------|-----------|\n| S3 IAM Role Config | Individual attributes | `assume_role` block | Update backend config |\n| S3 State Locking | DynamoDB required | DynamoDB or S3-native (experimental) | Optional: add `use_lockfile` |\n| Moved Block Syntax | No prefix needed | `resource.` prefix required for reserved keywords | Update moved blocks |\n| Sensitive Mark Propagation | Could be lost in conditionals | Always preserved | Remove workarounds |\n| `issensitive()` Function | Returns false for unknown | Returns unknown | Update conditionals |\n| Ephemeral Variables | Not supported | Supported | Use for temporary secrets |\n| Ephemeral Resources | Not supported | Supported | For provider use |\n\n---\n\n## Additional block syntax\n\n3. **Test in a non-production environment first**\n\n4. **Consult the Terraform community:**\n   - Terraform Registry discussions\n   - HashiCorp Community Forum\n   - GitHub Issues\n\n5. **Review your provider documentation:**\n   - Some providers may have specific migration guidance\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Before/After Configuration Examples\n\n### Complete S3 Backend Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.9.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                          = \"prod-terraform-state\"\n    key                             = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                          = \"us-east-1\"\n    encrypt                         = true\n    dynamodb_table                  = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # Deprecated IAM role assumption\n    role_arn                        = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformProdRole\"\n    session_name                    = \"terraform-prod\"\n    external_id                     = \"12345-abcde\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds    = 1800\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"Production\"\n      Team        = \"Infrastructure\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"prod-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n    encrypt = true\n\n    # Use assume_role block (DynamoDB still supported)\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # New assume_role block syntax\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformProdRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-prod\"\n      external_id = \"12345-abcde\"\n      duration    = \"30m\"\n\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"Production\"\n        Team        = \"Infrastructure\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Complete Moved Block Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\n# Regular resource moves (still work the same)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_web_server\n  to   = aws_instance.new_web_server\n}\n\n# These would work but generate errors in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_config       # Ambiguous\n  to   = local.new_config       # Ambiguous\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_app\n  to   = module.new_app  # This is correct (modules are modules)\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\n# Regular resource moves (unchanged)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_web_server\n  to   = aws_instance.new_web_server\n}\n\n# Resources with reserved keyword type names need resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_config\n  to   = resource.local.new_config\n}\n\n# Module moves remain unchanged\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_app\n  to   = module.new_app\n}\n\n# Data source moves\nmoved {\n  from = data.aws_ami.old\n  to   = data.aws_ami.new\n}\n```\n\n### Sensitive Values Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\n# Workaround needed to preserve sensitive mark\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  # Had to wrap in sensitive() to ensure mark wasn't lost\n  value       = sensitive(var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.db_password : \"default\")\n  description = \"Database password\"\n}\n\n# Using issensitive() required handling only true/false\nlocals {\n  is_sensitive = issensitive(var.db_password)\n\n  config = is_sensitive ? {\n    masked = true\n  } : {\n    masked = false\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\n# No workaround needed - marks propagate automatically\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.db_password : \"default\"\n  description = \"Database password\"\n}\n\n# issensitive() now returns unknown for unknown values\nlocals {\n  is_sensitive = issensitive(var.db_password)\n\n  # Need to handle unknown result\n  config = is_sensitive == true ? {\n    masked = true\n  } : is_sensitive == false ? {\n    masked = false\n  } : {\n    # Handle unknown case\n    masked = null\n  }\n}\n\n# For ephemeral secrets, use new feature\nvariable \"temporary_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  ephemeral = true  # Never persists to state\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated:** March 2026\n**Terraform Version:** v1.10.0\n**Compatibility:** Covers migration from v1.9.0 to
