This guide covers the breaking changes and migration steps required to upgrade from v1.9.0 to v1.10.0.\n\n**Key themes:**\n- S3 backend configuration simplification with new `assume_role` block syntax\n- Enhanced `moved` block functionality requiring explicit resource type qualification for reserved keywords\n- Improved sensitive value propagation in conditional expressions\n- Introduction of ephemeral input variables, outputs, and resources for secure secret handling\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend IAM Role Assumption Attributes Deprecated\n\n#### What Changed\n\nThe S3 backend in v1.9.0 used individual attributes for IAM role assumption:\n- `role_arn`\n- `session_name`\n- `external_id`\n- `assume_role_duration_seconds`\n- `assume_role_policy`\n- `assume_role_policy_arns`\n- `assume_role_tags`\n- `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys`\n\nAll these attributes are **deprecated as of v1.10.0** and will be removed in a future version. They are replaced by the new `assume_role` nested block.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nThe `assume_role` block provides:\n- Better schema organization and validation\n- Support for new features like `source_identity`\n- Consistent with other AWS provider block patterns\n- Clearer intent through block structure rather than prefixed attributes\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                          = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                             = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                          = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn                        = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                    = \"terraform\"\n    external_id                     = \"unique-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds    = 3600\n    assume_role_policy              = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Purpose = \"Terraform\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      duration    = \"1h\"\n      external_id = \"unique-external-id\"\n      policy      = jsonencode({...})\n\n      tags = {\n        Purpose = \"Terraform\"\n      }\n\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Purpose\"]\n\n      # New in v1.10.0: Specify source identity for the assumed role\n      source_identity = \"terraform-automation\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify all S3 backends using the deprecated attributes:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"role_arn\\|session_name\\|external_id\\|assume_role_duration\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update your backend configuration:**\n   - Replace individual `assume_role_*` attributes with the `assume_role` block\n   - Convert `assume_role_duration_seconds` to `duration` using time duration format (e.g., \"3600s\" or \"1h\")\n   - Note: `session_name` is now `session_name` within the block (attribute name unchanged)\n   - `assume_role_policy` becomes `policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` becomes `policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` becomes `tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` becomes `transitive_tag_keys`\n\n3. **Test the new configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -upgrade\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Duration Format:** The new `duration` attribute requires string values in time format. Use \"1h\", \"30m\", or \"3600s\" instead of seconds as a number.\n- **Missing scope:** If you have other IAM settings, ensure they're still included (e.g., `access_key`, `secret_key`, or AWS credential chain)\n- **Validation changes:** The `assume_role` block has stricter validation. All ARNs must follow proper AWS ARN format.\n\n#### Deprecation Timeline\n\n- v1.10.0: Deprecated (still works with deprecation warnings)\n- Future version: Will be removed entirely\n\n---\n\n### 2. New S3 Native State Locking Support (Experimental)\n\n#### What Changed\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces experimental support for S3-native state locking without requiring DynamoDB. This is controlled by the new `use_lockfile` attribute.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"  # Required for state locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Option 1: Keep DynamoDB\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket         = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key            = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region         = \"us-east-1\"\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Option 2: Use S3 Native Locking (Experimental)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket        = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key           = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region        = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile  = true  # Enable S3-native locking\n    # Note: omit dynamodb_table when using use_lockfile\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\nTo migrate from DynamoDB to S3 native locking:\n\n1. **Enable `use_lockfile` in your backend configuration:**\n   ```hcl\n   terraform {\n     backend \"s3\" {\n       use_lockfile = true\n     }\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Test with `terraform plan` first** (doesn't acquire state lock):\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n3. **Perform a state refresh** to verify locking works:\n   ```bash\n   terraform refresh\n   ```\n\n4. **Once verified, you can optionally remove the DynamoDB reference:**\n   - Remove `dynamodb_table` attribute\n   - Delete the DynamoDB table if no longer needed\n\n#### Compatibility Notes\n\n- **Experimental Status:** This feature is marked as experimental and may change in future releases\n- **Backwards Compatibility:** If both `dynamodb_table` and `use_lockfile` are specified, `dynamodb_table` takes precedence\n- **Permissions:** Requires `s3:GetObject`, `s3:PutObject`, and `s3:DeleteObject` permissions on the state file object\n\n---\n\n### 3. Moved Blocks Now Require \"resource.\" Prefix for Reserved Keywords\n\n#### What Changed\n\nWhen using `moved` blocks to refactor resource locations, if your resource type name matches a top-level Terraform keyword (like `resource`, `module`, `data`, `variable`, `local`, etc.), you must now explicitly prepend `resource.` to disambiguate it.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nWithout the explicit prefix, Terraform couldn't distinguish between:\n- A resource with type name \"module\" (e.g., `resource \"module\" \"example\"`)\n- A reference to a module (e.g., `module.example`)\n\nThe `resource.` prefix makes the intent unambiguous.\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0)\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = module.example\n  to   = aws_instance.example\n}\n\n# This was ambiguous for resource types matching keywords:\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_name      # Is this a local variable or a resource?\n  to   = custom_module.new   # Is this a module or a resource?\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0)\n\nFor resources with type names matching reserved keywords, prepend `resource.`:\n\n```hcl\n# Moving a resource type named \"local\" - must use resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n\n# Moving a resource type named \"module\" - must use resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.module.old_instance\n  to   = resource.module.new_instance\n}\n\n# Regular moves (non-keyword resource types) still work without prefix\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old\n  to   = aws_instance.new\n}\n\n# Module moves always use the \"module\" keyword (not resource.module)\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_module\n  to   = module.new_module\n}\n```\n\n#### Reserved Keywords Requiring \"resource.\" Prefix\n\nThe following keywords require the `resource.` prefix when used as resource type names:\n\n- `resource`\n- `data`\n- `module`\n- `variable`\n- `local`\n- `output`\n- `terraform`\n- `provider`\n- `moved`\n- `removed`\n- `import`\n- `path`\n- `self`\n- `count`\n- `each`\n- `template`\n- `lazy`\n- `arg`\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Identify moved blocks that reference reserved keywords:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -A 1 \"moved {\" *.tf | grep -E \"from|to.*\\s+(local|module|data|resource|variable|output|path|self|count|each|terraform|provider|template|lazy|arg)\\.\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update the affected moved blocks:**\n   - If the resource type name is a reserved keyword, add `resource.` prefix to both `from` and `to` addresses\n   - Examples:\n     ```hcl\n     # Before\n     moved {\n       from = local.example\n       to   = local.moved_example\n     }\n\n     # After\n     moved {\n       from = resource.local.example\n       to   = resource.local.moved_example\n     }\n     ```\n\n3. **Verify the configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **Module moves don't need \"resource.\":** Moving modules still uses `module.old_module` syntax, not `resource.module.old_module`\n- **Data sources don't use \"resource.\":** Data sources use `data.type.name` syntax naturally\n- **Only for resource type names:** The prefix is only needed when the resource *type* matches a keyword, not when moving from non-keyword types\n\n#### Error Message Example\n\nIf you forget to use `resource.` prefix:\n\n```\nError: Invalid \"moved\" addresses\n\nThe keyword \"local\" is reserved and cannot be used to target a resource\naddress. If you are targeting a resource type that uses a reserved keyword,\nplease prefix your address with \"resource.\".\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed\n\nIn v1.9.0, sensitive marks could be lost when values flowed through conditional (ternary) expressions. In v1.10.0, sensitive marks are properly propagated through all branches of conditional expressions, even when branches contain unknown values.\n\n#### Why This Changed\n\nTo prevent accidental exposure of sensitive values and to ensure consistent behavior between plan and apply phases.\n\n**Related Issue:** #36017\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0) - Marks Could Be Lost\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"prod\"\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0, the sensitive mark could be lost in this conditional\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.database_password : \"default-password\"\n  description = \"This might NOT be marked sensitive due to the conditional!\"\n}\n```\n\nIn v1.9.0, if one branch was unknown, Terraform might lose the sensitive mark from the other branch.\n\n#### After (v1.10.0) - Marks Are Always Preserved\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"database_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"prod\"\n}\n\n# In v1.10.0, the sensitive mark is properly preserved\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.database_password : \"default-password\"\n  description = \"This is now correctly marked sensitive!\"\n}\n```\n\nThe output `db_password` is correctly marked as sensitive, even though one branch is a literal string.\n\n#### Migration Steps\n\n1. **Review conditional expressions that work with sensitive values:**\n   ```bash\n   grep -r \"?\\|:\" *.tf | grep -i \"password\\|secret\\|key\\|token\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Update `sensitive()` function usage if needed:**\n\n   In v1.9.0, you might have worked around mark loss:\n   ```hcl\n   # v1.9.0 workaround (no longer needed)\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = sensitive(var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.secret : \"fallback\")\n   }\n   ```\n\n   In v1.10.0, this is still valid but unnecessary:\n   ```hcl\n   # v1.10.0 - marks now propagate automatically\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.secret : \"fallback\"\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Update logic using `issensitive()` function:**\n\n   In v1.9.0:\n   ```hcl\n   if issensitive(my_var) {\n     # Assume it's definitely sensitive\n   }\n   ```\n\n   In v1.10.0, `issensitive()` returns `unknown` for unknown values:\n   ```hcl\n   # Update your logic to handle unknown results\n   value = issensitive(my_var)\n   # value could now be true, false, or unknown\n   ```\n\n4. **Handle ephemeral values in conditionals:**\n\n   New in v1.10.0 - use `ephemeralasnull()` to replace ephemeral values:\n   ```hcl\n   # Replace ephemeral values with non-ephemeral nulls for persistence\n   output \"value\" {\n     value = ephemeralasnull(var.ephemeral_secret)\n  }\n   ```\n\n#### Impact on Plan Output\n\nWith improved mark propagation, Terraform state files may now show more values as sensitive than before. This is more correct behavior. For example:\n\n```diff\n# Before (v1.9.0)\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value = \"MyPassword123\"  # Not marked sensitive (mark was lost)\n}\n\n# After (v1.10.0)\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value = \"***\"  # Correctly marked sensitive\n}\n```\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- **`issensitive()` behavior change:** It now returns unknown for unknown inputs instead of false. Update any conditional logic that depends on this function.\n- **Type conversion functions:** Functions like `tostring()`, `tonumber()`, `tobool()` now preserve marks through conversions\n- **`nonsensitive()` function:** Use this explicitly if you need to remove the sensitive mark\n  ```hcl\n  output \"raw_password\" {\n    value = nonsensitive(var.database_password)\n  }\n  ```\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 5. Ephemeral Input Variables and Outputs\n\n#### What Is It?\n\nEphemeral values are a new category in Terraform that exist only in memory during a single Terraform phase (plan or apply) and are never persisted to state files, plans, or outputs. This is useful for short-lived secrets, tokens, or credentials that should not appear in any artifacts.\n\n#### Usage\n\n**Ephemeral Input Variables:**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n  sensitive = true\n}\n```\n\n**Ephemeral Outputs:**\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value     = local_sensitive_data.credentials\n  ephemeral = true  # New in v1.10.0\n}\n```\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n- **Not persisted:** Never written to state, plan files, or saved outputs\n- **Single phase only:** Values are discarded after the current phase (plan or apply) completes\n- **Use in provider configs:** Primarily intended for provider configurations and provisioners\n- **Cannot be referenced by non-ephemeral outputs:** Ephemeral values cannot flow into persistent outputs\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\nIf you have sensitive values that should never persist:\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  # Still gets written to state file\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  ephemeral = true\n  # Never gets written to state file\n}\n```\n\n#### When to Use Ephemeral\n\nUse ephemeral for:\n- API tokens that expire quickly\n- Temporary credentials from STS AssumeRole\n- One-time passwords or codes\n- Session tokens\n\nDo NOT use ephemeral for:\n- Database passwords (need persistence for apply)\n- SSH keys (need persistence)\n- Regular sensitive data (use `sensitive = true`)\n\n#### Example: Ephemeral Variables with Assume Role\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. Ephemeral Resources\n\n#### What Is It?\n\nEphemeral resources are a new resource mode for opening short-lived connections or sessions. Unlike managed resources (which are created and stored in state), ephemeral resources:\n- Exist only during the current Terraform phase\n- Don't persist to state\n- Are automatically closed when the phase completes\n- Support renewal if their expiration time is approached\n\n#### Usage\n\nEphemeral resources are used in provider plugins and are less commonly used directly in configuration, but you might see them referenced in provider documentation:\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_assume_role_session\" \"provider_auth\" {\n  role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/ProviderRole\"\n  session_name = \"terraform-provider\"\n  duration_seconds = 900\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  # Use ephemeral credentials from the assumed role\n  assume_role {\n    role_arn = ephemeral.aws_assume_role_session.provider_auth.role_arn\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Impact\n\n- **For most users:** No direct migration needed\n- **For provider developers:** May need to implement ephemeral resource support\n- **Existing configurations:** Not affected unless explicitly using ephemeral resources\n\n#### Key Features\n\n- **Automatic cleanup:** Closed automatically after phase completion\n- **Renewal support:** Providers can request renewal before expiration\n- **Prevents state explosion:** Temporary resources don't clutter the state file\n- **Secret protection:** Credentials don't persist in any artifacts\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\n### Pre-Migration Testing\n\n1. **Run validation on current configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan -out=backup.plan\n   ```\n\n2. **Check for deprecated patterns:**\n   ```bash\n   # Look for S3 backend IAM attributes\n   grep -r \"assume_role_\\|role_arn.*backend\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n\n   # Look for moved blocks with reserved keywords\n   grep -B 1 -A 1 \"moved.*local\\.\\|moved.*module\\.\" . --include=\"*.tf\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Review sensitive variable usage:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform console\n\n   # Try accessing sensitive outputs\n   > output.my_output  # Should show ***\n   ```\n\n### Migration Checklist\n\n- [ ] Backup current state file\n- [ ] Update S3 backend configuration if using deprecated IAM attributes\n- [ ] Update `moved` blocks to use `resource.` prefix for reserved keywords\n- [ ] Test the upgraded backend configuration\n- [ ] Review sensitive value handling in conditionals\n- [ ] Plan changes after upgrade\n- [ ] Apply changes with no resource modifications expected\n- [ ] Verify state file integrity\n- [ ] Test rollback procedures\n\n### Testing Commands\n\n```bash\n# Initialize with new backend (test connection)\nterraform init -upgrade\n\n# Validate configuration\nterraform validate\n\n# Generate plan (should have no changes)\nterraform plan -detailed-exitcode\n# Expected: exit code 0 (no changes)\n\n# Review state integrity\nterraform show\n\n# List all resources to verify they're intact\nterraform state list\n```\n\n### Validation Testing\n\nTest that sensitive marks are preserved:\n\n```hcl\n# test.tf\nvariable \"secret_value\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  default   = \"my-secret\"\n}\n\nvariable \"use_default\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = true\n}\n\noutput \"test_mark\" {\n  value       = var.use_default ? var.secret_value : \"fallback\"\n  description = \"Should be marked sensitive\"\n}\n\noutput \"check_mark\" {\n  value = issensitive(var.secret_value)\n}\n```\n\n```bash\nterraform init\nterraform apply\nterraform show  # Verify output shows \"***\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\n### If Migration Fails\n\n1. **Restore from backup:**\n   ```bash\n   # If you have a backup of terraform.tfstate\n   cp terraform.tfstate.backup terraform.tfstate\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes:**\n   ```bash\n   git checkout HEAD -- .  # If using git\n   ```\n\n3. **Downgrade Terraform version:**\n   ```bash\n   # If necessary, downgrade back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version\n\n   # Remove v1.10.0 binary and reinstall v1.9.0\n   # Process depends on your installation method\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify state consistency:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n### Reverting S3 Backend Changes\n\nIf you need to revert the `assume_role` block back to individual attributes:\n\n```hcl\n# Current (v1.10.0) - assume_role block\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-state\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      duration    = \"1h\"\n      external_id = \"my-external-id\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n# Revert to (v1.9.0) - individual attributes\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                       = \"my-state\"\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform\"\n    external_id                  = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n  }\n}\n\n# Then reinitialize\nterraform init\n```\n\n### Reverting Moved Block Changes\n\nIf you need to revert `moved` blocks with `resource.` prefix:\n\n```hcl\n# Current (v1.10.0) - with resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_value\n  to   = resource.local.new_value\n}\n\n# Simply remove the resource. prefix to revert\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_value\n  to   = local.new_value\n}\n```\n\nNote: After reverting, these will produce errors until you downgrade to v1.9.0.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n| Feature | v1.9.0 | v1.10.0 | Migration |\n|---------|--------|---------|-----------|\n| S3 IAM Role Config | Individual attributes | `assume_role` block | Update backend config |\n| S3 State Locking | DynamoDB required | DynamoDB or S3-native (experimental) | Optional: add `use_lockfile` |\n| Moved Block Syntax | No prefix needed | `resource.` prefix required for reserved keywords | Update moved blocks |\n| Sensitive Mark Propagation | Could be lost in conditionals | Always preserved | Remove workarounds |\n| `issensitive()` Function | Returns false for unknown | Returns unknown | Update conditionals |\n| Ephemeral Variables | Not supported | Supported | Use for temporary secrets |\n| Ephemeral Resources | Not supported | Supported | For provider use |\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Terraform v1.10.0 Release Notes](https://www.terraform.io/docs/language/settings/backends/s3.html)\n- [S3 Backend Configuration Documentation](https://www.terraform.io/docs/language/settings/backends/s3.html)\n- [Moved Block Documentation](https://www.terraform.io/docs/language/state/moved.html)\n- [Sensitive Values Documentation](https://www.terraform.io/docs/language/values/outputs.html#sensitive)\n- [Ephemeral Values Documentation](https://www.terraform.io/docs/language/values/variables.html#ephemeral)\n\n---\n\n## Getting Help\n\nIf you encounter issues during migration:\n\n1. **Check the Terraform version:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform version\n   ```\n\n2. **Review error messages carefully:**\n   - Look for \"reserved keyword\" errors → add `resource.` prefix\n   - Look for \"deprecated\" warnings → use new block syntax\n\n3. **Test in a non-production environment first**\n\n4. **Consult the Terraform community:**\n   - Terraform Registry discussions\n   - HashiCorp Community Forum\n   - GitHub Issues\n\n5. **Review your provider documentation:**\n   - Some providers may have specific migration guidance\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: Before/After Configuration Examples\n\n### Complete S3 Backend Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.9.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket                          = \"prod-terraform-state\"\n    key                             = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region                          = \"us-east-1\"\n    encrypt                         = true\n    dynamodb_table                  = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # Deprecated IAM role assumption\n    role_arn                        = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformProdRole\"\n    session_name                    = \"terraform-prod\"\n    external_id                     = \"12345-abcde\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds    = 1800\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"Production\"\n      Team        = \"Infrastructure\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  required_version = \">= 1.10.0\"\n\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"prod-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n    encrypt = true\n\n    # Use assume_role block (DynamoDB still supported)\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-locks\"\n\n    # New assume_role block syntax\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn    = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformProdRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-prod\"\n      external_id = \"12345-abcde\"\n      duration    = \"30m\"\n\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"Production\"\n        Team        = \"Infrastructure\"\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Complete Moved Block Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\n# Regular resource moves (still work the same)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_web_server\n  to   = aws_instance.new_web_server\n}\n\n# These would work but generate errors in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.old_config       # Ambiguous\n  to   = local.new_config       # Ambiguous\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_app\n  to   = module.new_app  # This is correct (modules are modules)\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\n# Regular resource moves (unchanged)\nmoved {\n  from = aws_instance.old_web_server\n  to   = aws_instance.new_web_server\n}\n\n# Resources with reserved keyword type names need resource. prefix\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_config\n  to   = resource.local.new_config\n}\n\n# Module moves remain unchanged\nmoved {\n  from = module.old_app\n  to   = module.new_app\n}\n\n# Data source moves\nmoved {\n  from = data.aws_ami.old\n  to   = data.aws_ami.new\n}\n```\n\n### Sensitive Values Migration Example\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\n# Workaround needed to preserve sensitive mark\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  # Had to wrap in sensitive() to ensure mark wasn't lost\n  value       = sensitive(var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.db_password : \"default\")\n  description = \"Database password\"\n}\n\n# Using issensitive() required handling only true/false\nlocals {\n  is_sensitive = issensitive(var.db_password)\n\n  config = is_sensitive ? {\n    masked = true\n  } : {\n    masked = false\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\n# No workaround needed - marks propagate automatically\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  value       = var.environment == \"prod\" ? var.db_password : \"default\"\n  description = \"Database password\"\n}\n\n# issensitive() now returns unknown for unknown values\nlocals {\n  is_sensitive = issensitive(var.db_password)\n\n  # Need to handle unknown result\n  config = is_sensitive == true ? {\n    masked = true\n  } : is_sensitive == false ? {\n    masked = false\n  } : {\n    # Handle unknown case\n    masked = null\n  }\n}\n\n# For ephemeral secrets, use new feature\nvariable \"temporary_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  ephemeral = true  # Never persists to state\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n**Last Updated:** March 2026\n**Terraform Version:** v1.10.0\n**Compatibility:** Covers migration from v1.9.0 to v1.10.0\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
